Summary 
The basic purpose of this study is a fair comparison of CPA and PC-SAFT Equations of State 
in well-defined ternary systems, containing Aliphatic & Aromatic hydrocarbons, Water, Methanol, 
Ethanol and MEG, as well as the individual evaluation of the two models. More specifically, high 
priority will be given to the modeling of systems containing the following hydrocarbons: Methane, 
Hexane, Benzene and Toluene. 
Considering the great interest of oil & gas industry in hydrate inhibitor systems, the 
applicability of CPA and PC-SAFT EoS, in terms of accuracy and predictive correlation between 
experimental and modeling phase equilibrium data, will be investigated. 
Literature review will be conducted for obtaining the experimental phase equilibrium data, as 
well as the modeling parameters and approaches. The required binary interaction parameters for the 
modeling of the ternary systems will be found either through literature review or will be obtained by 
modeling the corresponding binary systems in this work. 
Finally, in this study, an overall fair comparison between CPA and PC-SAFT EoS will be 
conducted and possible suggestions, in order to improve the predictive performance of the models, 
will be demonstrated.

Chapter 1: Introduction 
It is an undeniable fact that thermodynamic data and particularly phase equilibrium data are 
crucial for petroleum and chemical industries. However, there are also additional fields that are 
interested in such kind of thermodynamic data like environmental and material science as well. The 
use of such kind of data is mostly involved in oil & gas and chemical companies, however the 
implementation of thermodynamic tools becomes more and more important nowadays for several 
different sectors apart from the aforementioned ones. Thus, it has observed an increasing use of 
thermodynamic data and models also in pharmaceutical companies and for environmental 
assessments as well. Furthermore, it has to be taken into consideration the fact that there are many 
unit operations, in which the knowledge and use of phase equilibrium data, is the basic requirement 
for the accomplishment of the processes. Such unit operations are distillation & extraction, adsorption 
& absorption, bio-separation and crystallization processes as well. [1] 
 
All calculations, containing phase equilibrium data, have the same key or beginning 
point, the concept of “iso-fugacity”, which means that the fugacities of all components of the 
corresponding system in any of the phases are equal. Consequently, on that principle are based all 
equations of state and thermodynamic models, which have been created and developed in order to 
perform phase equilibrium calculations. These equations of state are the thermodynamic models, 
which are created in such a way to be able to describe the systems of interest (binaries, ternaries & 
multi-components). These thermodynamic models are mostly expressed in P(V,T) functions or 
V(P,T). [1] 
 
The vast majority of the conducted processes in all oil & gas related industries are 
dealing with a wide range of different types of systems, others more important and others with lower 
importance. A system or mixture can be classified as very important or less important, according to 
its nature, which can be characterized from “complexity” or “simplicity”. Whether a mixture is 
characterized with the term “complexity” or “simplicity” is based on the components that are involved 
in it. Thus, in the absence of associating components, a system can be considered as simple, whereas 
the presence of associating compounds (e.g. Water, Glycols, Alcohols, Amines, Acids, etc.), which 
are capable of creating hydrogen bonds, can label the mixture in the complex category. Regarding 
the 2nd category with the associating mixtures, it has been observed a difficulty in the prediction of 
their Vapor-Liquid Equilibria and consequently it has been conducted scientific research in order to 
overcome the difficulties and to predict more accurately and precisely the aforementioned phase 
==PAGE:20==
Technical University of Denmark 
 
20 
 
equilibria. In that “complex” category are included also the systems that are described as cross-
associating, self-associating or include both polar and non-polar compounds. Therefore, in order to 
be achieved an accurate description of such systems, apart from the use of the “simple” cubic 
equations of state with their corresponding mixing rules, there have been developed more advanced 
non-cubic equations of state. [2] 
The systems of interest in this study are the hydrate inhibitor systems, which contain Aliphatic 
& Aromatic hydrocarbons, Water and the thermodynamic hydrate inhibitors Methanol, Ethanol or 
MEG. Considering the presence of polar components within an under investigation system, this fact 
disables the possibility to use the cubic equations of state without certain additional advanced mixing 
rules. Therefore, more advanced models have been developed in order to be able to describe and 
correlate the phase equilibria data of complex systems as well. More specifically, the Cubic-Plus-
Association Equation of State (CPA EoS) [6],[7] and the Statistical Associating Fluid Theory (SAFT 
EoS) in general or more particularly in some special versions of it (e.g. PC-SAFT [8],[9] or sPC-
SAFT [11]), have been applied in systems containing hydrocarbons with polar and associating 
components. [1] 
Throughout the last decades, petroleum and chemical industries have considerably improved 
their methodology used and this fact is due to the recent development, which has been achieved in 
the thermodynamic field and in particular in the applied thermodynamic models. The need to 
overcome the observed limitations and difficulties that the conventional models presented led to the 
implementation of new more advanced equations of state, more capable in describing also the 
complex mixtures. The further development of the thermodynamic tools (models and equations of 
state), e.g. CPA EoS and PC-SAFT EoS, is probably going to continue take place in the following 
years in terms of accuracy and efficiency. Furthermore, most industrial sectors, including the oil 
industries, try apart from accuracy and efficiency to achieve more environmental friendly processes 
and the aforementioned development of the thermodynamic models is going to help also this goal. 
Finally, considering all these potential improvements and developments in the thermodynamic field 
and in particular the accurate prediction of phase equilibria data, the changes and the implementation 
of the new methodology will be applied even to the most immature sectors of the chemical 
engineering field.  [1] 
The basic purpose of this study is a fair comparison of CPA and PC-SAFT Equations of State 
in well – defined ternary systems, containing Aliphatic & Aromatic hydrocarbons, Water, Methanol, 
==PAGE:21==
Modeling of Thermodynamics of Hydrate Inhibitor Systems 
 
21 
 
Ethanol and MEG, as well as the individual evaluation of the two models. More specifically, high 
priority will be given to the modeling of systems containing Methane, Hexane, Benzene and Toluene. 
Considering the great interest of the oil & gas industry in hydrate inhibitor systems, the applicability 
of CPA and PC-SAFT EoS, in terms of accuracy and predictive correlation between experimental 
and modeling phase equilibrium data, will be investigated. 
 
 
 
==PAGE:22==
Technical University of Denmark 
 
22 
 
1.1 
Theoretical Background 
1.1.1 Associating (hydrogen bonding) mixtures 
Associating or “in other words” hydrogen bonding mixtures are considered to have high 
importance in the petroleum and chemical industries. These systems contain components, which are 
capable of creating hydrogen bonds, like water, alcohols, amines, glycols, acids, etc. [1] 
Due to this hydrogen bonding phenomenon, such mixtures are considered as complex 
associating systems and their phase equilibria are important for several practical applications and 
cases. For example, mixtures containing water, glycols, alcohols and hydrocarbons are present in a 
wide range of chemical and hydrocarbon processes, e.g. in order to meet environmental legislations, 
by low emissions. [1] 
The alcohol or the glycol play the role of the co-solvent, improving significantly the mutual 
solubility of hydrocarbons and water in both phases (aqueous-rich phase and hydrocarbon-rich 
phase). In the absence of these aforementioned co-solvents, the mutual solubilities are considerably 
low. [1] 
Phase equilibria of such associating systems are important in many cases and some examples 
are demonstrated in order to show their implementation in the different sectors. Regarding the oil & 
gas industry, the formation of gas hydrates, with the corresponding calculations about the amount of 
the hydrate inhibitor that has to be used is one of the most important application of such phase 
equilibria. Furthermore, the improving of the gasoline’s Octane Number by adding alcohols and for 
environmental reasons, as well as the use of glycols (TEG) in regeneration units (gas dehydration). 
Apart from the oil industry, phase equilibria of associating systems are also used for environmental 
aspects, e.g. calculations of partition coefficients of water-octanol and etc. as well as for the waste 
streams modeling procedures. Considering the chemical industries, phase equilibria are used 
throughout separation methods and applications for pharmaceuticals. Finally, they are also used in 
polymer, biotechnology/biochemical, and food industries and for process design purposes as well.  
[1] 
By taking into consideration all the above-presented sectors and fields that the associating 
mixtures are involved, the importance of their corresponding phase equilibrium calculations are very 
important. More specifically throughout this study, the case of the hydrate inhibitor systems is going 
be investigated.  
==PAGE:23==
Modeling of Thermodynamics of Hydrate Inhibitor Systems 
 
23 
 
1.1.2 Hydrates & Hydrate Inhibition 
Hydrate formation is a possibility for a several procedures including in the oil & gas industry, 
from the beginning procedure of exploration for gas or oil and also for the operations that take place 
afterwards like production, transportation of the extracted product and processing of it in the end. 
This phenomenon in order to occur requires first of all the presence of the water molecule as well as 
other molecules, smaller than n-pentane. Considering this hydrate formation phenomenon, when 
small nonpolar molecules (smaller than 9 Å) are coming in contact with water molecules at ambient 
temperature conditions (usually lower than 310.93 K) and at moderate pressure conditions (usually 
higher than 12.4 Bar), a crystal water form might appear, the so-called “clathrate hydrate”. [3] 
Thereafter, a combination of the appropriate temperature and pressure conditions as well as 
the presence of gases with low molecular weight (e.g. Methane, Ethane, Propane, CO2, H2S, N2) may 
result water molecules to reform into coplanar poly-membered (5 or 6) rings and afterwards the 
creation of a 3D polyhedral shaped formations around the trapped gas. Thus, it can be noticed that 
the water acts like a cage and within it, there is trapped the guest-molecule (gas). This gas hydrate 
formation can be seen in the following figure, where in the middle is trapped the guest-molecule 
surrounded by the red structure, which is the water “cage”. [3],[4] 
 
Figure 1.1: Gas Hydrate Formation [4] 
 
This “hydrate formation” is considered as one of the most important problems in the oil 
& gas industries due to the fact that, when it occurs, it can reduce the flow of the gas in the pipeline 
and eventually block the pipeline stopping the production. Apart from the decrease of the gas flow in 
the pipeline, it can also affect and damage the equipment used increasing the extra costs of the 
production. [4] 
==PAGE:24==
Technical University of Denmark 
 
24 
 
 
Figure 1.2: A large gas hydrate plug formed in a subsea hydrocarbon pipeline (Picture from Petrobras – Brazil) [12] 
The most widely used techniques or methods to prevent hydrate formation in the oil and gas 
industries nowadays are based on the conditions of the hydrate formation concept. The most common 
ones are mentioned below [4]:  
i. 
Dehydration techniques in order to reduce the water concentration in the system 
ii. 
Maintenance of the temperature conditions above the 293.15 K by insulating or 
heating of the system 
iii. 
Likewise the previous one, maintenance of the pressure conditions below 10 Bars 
iv. 
Addition of salts or chemicals like alcohols and glycols as hydrate inhibitors 
Regarding this study, the focus will be given in the last presented way of preventing the 
hydrate formation phenomenon and the hydrate inhibitors that will be used in the phase equilibrium 
calculations in the modeling part will be Methanol, Ethanol and Mono-Ethylene Glycol (MEG). 
Considering the aforementioned hydrate inhibitors, MEG is the most widely used 
thermodynamic hydrate inhibitor (THI) nowadays by the oil & gas companies [4]. Both Methanol 
and MEG are effective and reliable in preventing the phenomenon, however MEG presents a crucial 
advantage over the Methanol, which is the fact that it can be reused and regenerated with insignificant 
losses. Another important advantage of using MEG as additive is the fact that decreases the possibility 
of creation and occurrence of corrosion in the pipelines. The Tri-Ethylene Glycol (TEG) is another 
thermodynamic hydrate inhibitor, which is used mostly to remove the free water that is responsible 
for the hydrate formation, due to its high viscosity. As for Methanol, it should be mentioned that this 
chemical in particular has used as a hydrate inhibitor from the time that the hydrate formation began 
to be known. As it was demonstrated before, Methanol lack in regenerated capability for reuse, due 
==PAGE:25==
Modeling of Thermodynamics of Hydrate Inhibitor Systems 
 
25 
 
to the high losses obtained throughout the process. However, in cases that the use of MEG did not 
provide the desired results, Methanol is the chemical that is injected to “finish the job”. So, 
considering the above-presented discussion about the chemicals used as additives for preventing the 
hydrate formation it can be concluded that both Methanol and MEG are efficient with a slight superior 
performance, however the cost of using Methanol is higher due to the regeneration that can be 
achieved in the MEG and its corresponding reuse in the system. [4] 
 
 
==PAGE:26==
Technical University of Denmark 
 
26 
 
1.2 
Thermodynamic Models 
In this study, the thermodynamic models that were used to model the phase equilibrium data, 
in order to be evaluated in terms of predicting capability and accuracy afterwards were the following 
two: 
 The Cubic-Plus-Association (CPA) 
 The Perturbed Chain - Statistical Associating Fluid Theory (PC-SAFT) 
Thus, in this section, the description of the two aforementioned equations of state is going to 
take place, before presenting the modeling work conducted and the results obtained, as well the 
corresponding discussion about them. Before the description of the PC-SAFT EoS, a brief 
introduction to the SAFT theory in general will take place as well. 
1.2.1 The Cubic-Plus-Association Equation of State (CPA EoS) 
The first thermodynamic model that was used in this study is the Cubic-Plus-Association 
Equation of State (CPA EoS) and was proposed by Kontogeorgis et al. [6],[7]  
This equation of state is a combination of Soave-Redlich-Kwong Equation of State (SRK 
EoS) with an additional special association term, which is based on the Wertheim’s theory. That 
special association term is likewise the SAFT theory, which is also described afterwards. The basic 
principle of the CPA EoS is that this model is capable to use the cubic equations of state when 
hydrogen bonding compounds are not present within the investigated mixture. On the other hand, in 
the case of presence of hydrogen bonding compounds in the under investigation mixture, CPA uses 
an association term of SAFT theory in order to be able to describe the association mixture. More 
specifically, the cubic SRK EoS accounts for the physical interactions that occur between the 
molecules, whereas the aforementioned special association term is introduced in order to account for 
specific interactions. Such specific interactions are interactions between the sites of the involving 
molecules, due to the creation of hydrogen bonds between “self-” or “cross-” associating molecules. 
Furthermore, it should also be mentioned that widely research has been conducted for developing the 
CPA EoS, in order to be capable of describing phase equilibria of “complex” mixtures in terms of 
efficiency and accuracy. “Complex” can be defined the mixtures, which contain apart from 
hydrocarbons also polar or associating components e.g. water, alcohols, glycols, esters and organic 
acids. [1],[5] 
==PAGE:27==
Modeling of Thermodynamics of Hydrate Inhibitor Systems 
 
27 
 
 
The expression of CPA, which was proposed from Kontogeorgis et al. [6],[7] for 
mixtures in terms of pressure is presented below:

In above-presented equation the term XAi is the most important part of the special 
association term and stands for the fraction of sites A of molecule i that are not forming bonds with 
the rest active sites. Moreover, another important part of the association term is the molar fraction of 
the component i, which is denoted as xi. [1]

However, there are also mixtures containing one self–associating component and an inert one, 
where occurs the possibility of solvation between the two components. CPA is capable of describing 
such mixtures including water, glycols or alcohols with aromatic hydrocarbons. For these “solvating 
mixtures”, by using experimental data the cross association volume can be optimized, whereas the 
cross-association energy parameter is just the half of the value of the associating component. 
 
1.2.2 The Statistical Associating Fluid Theory (SAFT Theory) 
SAFT is the abbreviation of the well-known Statistical Associating Fluid Theory, which is a 
theoretically – derived powerful model. This model is based on the perturbation theory and is a non-
cubic equation of state that takes into account all attractive, repulsive and hydrogen bonding forces 
as well. Chain effects are also taken into consideration by this theory. Likewise the association term 
of the CPA EoS, the chain and association terms of SAFT theory have their basis in the Wertheim’s 
theory. Regarding the repulsive and attractive/dispersion forces, the former ones are described with 
the hard-sphere equation, whereas the later ones are described by several models e.g. square well or 
Lennard-Jones. According to the different dispersion term there have created and developed several 
versions of the SAFT equation. In this study, the perturbed chain – statistical associating fluid theory 
(PC-SAFT) is going to be used in the modeling part, thus a description of this equation of state in 
particular it is going to take place afterwards. The SAFT model in general considers the involved 
molecules as being built into segments and therefore the interactions between these segments are the 
ones, which are under investigation. [1]  
The residual Helmholtz energy (αres) is described by the following equation: 
𝛼𝑟𝑒𝑠= 𝛼𝑠𝑒𝑔+ 𝛼𝑐ℎ𝑎𝑖𝑛+ 𝛼𝑎𝑠𝑠𝑜𝑐   (𝐸𝑞. 1.16) 
==PAGE:30==
Technical University of Denmark 
 
30 
 
 
Likewise the aforementioned CPA EoS, also SAFT EoS includes usually, five 
parameters in total, again three for non-associating components and two for associating components. 
All these parameters characterize each one of the pure compounds and are obtained by fitting vapor 
pressure and saturated liquid density as well. More specifically, these five parameters are listed below 
[1]: 
 Number of segments of the molecule, denoted as m 
 Diameter of the segment, denoted as σ 
 Depth of the dispersion potential (energy parameter), denoted as ε 
 Association energy between site A in molecule I with site B I molecule j, denoted as εAB 
 Association volume, denoted as κAB 
 
According to the SAFT theory, the formation of a molecule is accomplished in a four step 
procedure, which is described below step by step and with a schematic representation as well [1]: 
1st Step: The fluid is represented as equally size hard spheres (b) 
2nd Step: Attraction between these equally sized spheres by addition of a dispersive potential (c) 
3rd Step: Addition of chain sites lead to appearance of chain molecules (d) 
4th Step: Addition of specific interaction sites results in hydrogen bonding attractive 
interactions and consequently association of the chains (e) 
 
Figure 1.3: Procedure of forming a molecule according to the SAFT model [1] 
 
==PAGE:31==
Modeling of Thermodynamics of Hydrate Inhibitor Systems 
 
31 
 
1.2.3 The Perturbed Chain - Statistical Associating Fluid Theory (PC-SAFT EoS) 
One of the most widely used version of SAFT theory for modeling of complex phase equilibria 
is the perturbed chain – statistical associating fluid theory equation of state (PC-SAFT EoS). [8] This 
version of SAFT theory was introduced by J. Gross and G. Sadowski [9] and its simplified form by 
N. von Solms et al. [11]  
 This model, in particular, considers the molecules involved as chains composed of freely 
jointed segments, which have spherical shape. These segments may possess association sites, 
resulting in short range interactions e.g. hydrogen bonding interactions. The unique characteristic of 
the PC-SAFT model, among all rest versions of SAFT theory, is its fundamental difference regarding 
the dispersion term, which takes into account the attractive forces created by the dispersion between 
whole chains. These entire chains may also carry partial charges and these charges can be two for the 
dipolar segments or three if the segments are quadrupolar. The molecular model described by the PC-
SAFT EoS and its schematic representation as for the attractive interactions is illustrated below 
[1],[10]: 
 
Figure 1.4: Molecular model of the PC-SAFT EoS [10] 
PC-SAFT model divides the total intermolecular forces into two terms, a reference and a 
perturbation one. The former one stands for the hard-chain fluid, whereas the later one stands for the 
attractive intermolecular forces, which are further divided into some contribution terms. The 
expression of the residual Helmholtz energy, according to the model, is presented below:  
𝛼𝑟𝑒𝑠= 𝛼ℎ𝑐+ 𝛼𝑑𝑖𝑠𝑝+ 𝛼𝑎𝑠𝑠𝑜𝑐    (𝐸𝑞. 1.17) 
Likewise, SAFT theory in general and CPA as well, five pure-component parameters are 
existing. Three of them account for the non-polar or non-associating components and two additional 
==PAGE:32==
Technical University of Denmark 
 
32 
 
for the associating ones. The former three are the number of the segments, the size of the segment 
and the depth of the occurring pair potential as well. The “associating” parameters are crucial for this 
study, due to the existence of systems, involving polar or associating compounds. Thereafter, the 
association energy and the effective association volume parameters have also to be introduced for the 
components of relevance. [10]

Modeling of Thermodynamics of Hydrate Inhibitor Systems

Chapter 2: Literature Review 
The basic purpose of this study is the modeling of thermodynamics of hydrate inhibitor 
systems, thus a literature review of experimental phase equilibrium data had to be conducted in 
advance for the systems that are of interest. Apart from these experimental data, which were used for 
the modeling part, another literature review regarding the modeling work that has been done so far 
by using the CPA and PC-SAFT EoS for ternary and multicomponent systems was conducted as well.  
2.1 
Literature Review for Phase Equilibrium Data 
The systems that were investigated throughout this study were hydrate inhibitor systems, 
thereafter experimental phase equilibrium data were collected for ternary & multicomponent systems 
containing Aliphatic & Aromatic Hydrocarbons, Water and Mono-Ethylene Glycol (MEG), Methanol 
or Ethanol. In addition, systems containing Tri-Ethylene Glycol (TEG) instead of MEG or Methanol 
were also included in the following phase equilibrium data collection, but these systems will not be 
used in the modeling part. 
The phase equilibrium data, which were collected during this literature review, for both 
ternary and multi-component systems, included temperature (T) and pressure (P) conditions, liquid 
(x) and vapor (y) molar compositions. 
The components of the systems found, through this literature review, are mentioned (with 
their chemical formula) below: Methane (CH4), Ethane (C2H6), Propane (C3H8), Butane (C4H10), 
Hexane (C6H14), Heptane (C7H16), Octane (C8H18), Nonane (C9H20), Decane (C10H22), Benzene 
(C6H6), Toluene (C7H8), Ethylbenzene (C8H10), Water (H2O), Methanol (MeOH - CH4O), Ethanol 
(EtOH – C2H6O), Mono-Ethylene Glycol (MEG – C2H6O2) and Tri-Ethylene Glycol (TEG – 
C6H14O4). 
In the following tables, the phase equilibrium data collected (36 ternary + 10 multicomponent 
systems) are summarized in brief, whereas the entire tables, including all information about the 
corresponding data, are provided in the Appendix I.

2.2 
Literature Review for CPA and PC-SAFT EoS 
This literature investigation was conducted for the evaluation of the performance and accuracy 
of both CPA and PC-SAFT models, when applied to systems containing Aliphatic and Aromatic 
Hydrocarbons, Water, Methanol, Ethanol and Mono-Ethylene Glycol (MEG). The evaluation of the 
performance of both models, when applied in ternary and multicomponent systems containing the 
aforementioned components, is the basic purpose of this study and in order to accomplish such 
evaluation all the research done so far on this field should be taken into consideration.  
Thereafter, in the following tables (Table 2.3 & Table 2.4) are presented the binary and 
ternary/multi-component systems found throughout the literature review respectively. In both tables 
are included the type of phase equilibria of each system and the models, which were used from the 
different groups of authors. Furthermore, there are also presented afterwards two tables (Table 2.5 & 
Table 2.6) including the average deviations obtained by the corresponding authors for binary systems 
containing the components of interest for this study. The detailed tables, with all deviations included 
and all interaction parameters as well, are provided in the Appendix II.  
Finally, the deviations of ternary systems containing the components of interest are presented 
in the end (Table 2.7).

Considering all the papers found throughout the literature review, regarding the performance 
and applicability of CPA and PC-SAFT EoS in hydrate inhibitor systems over a wide range of 
temperature conditions, the following conclusions and observations were extracted. 
First of all, as it can be noticed from Table 2.3 & Table 2.4, the vast majority of hydrate 
inhibitor systems found were modeled by using the CPA EoS. Regarding the binary systems, it was 
found that both CPA and PC-SAFT were used in order to predict the phase equilibria, whereas the 
ternary and multi-component ones that were modeled exclusively by the CPA EoS, according to the 
literature review. Thus, it can be concluded that there is no straightforward comparison of the 
performance of the two models in hydrate inhibitor systems. Due to the significant importance of 
such mixtures in the oil & gas industry, this study will focus on accomplishing a fair comparison as 
for the applicability and performance of both CPA and PC-SAFT EoS in the aforementioned systems 
of interest. 
Regarding the binary systems first, several groups of authors conducted modeling work of 
Water-Methanol and Water-Ethanol systems, as can be observed through Table 2.5. As for Water-
Methanol, it can be seen from the same table that CPA EoS by using either CR-1 or ECR combining 
rules with temperature dependent interaction parameters can perform very satisfactorily. The obtained 
average percentage deviation for bubble point pressure was ranged from 1.3 up to 1.6 % according to 
Tybjerg et al. [23] and Folas et al. [28] and the corresponding deviation for the vapor-phase mole 
fraction was 0.007 according to both aforementioned groups of authors. Considering the same system 
Water-Methanol and by using one temperature independent interaction parameter (-0.09) with ECR 
combining rules, the CPA EoS can perform also satisfactorily, indicating an average percentage 
deviation of 2.6 % as for the bubble point pressure and 0.011 as for the vapor-phase mole fraction, 
according to Kontogeorgis et al. [24], [30] and Folas et al. [28]. Similarly very good predictive results 
were obtained for the system Water-Ethanol by using the CPA EoS with both CR-1 and ECR 
combining rules. By using temperature dependent and independent (-0.11) interaction parameters, 
CPA provides very good predictions of the bubble point pressure and the vapor-phase mole fraction, 
indicating deviations around 1.9 % and 0.01 - 0.013 respectively, according to Kontogeorgis et al. 
[24], [30] and Voutsas et al. [28]. 
Apart from Methanol or Ethanol with Water, other important binary systems for this study are 
the ones containing Benzene, Toluene, MEG and Water. By taking into consideration the Table 2.6, 
it can be concluded that CPA EoS with BETCR combining rules can perform well predicting the 
==PAGE:43==
Modeling of Thermodynamics of Hydrate Inhibitor Systems 
 
43 
 
Water solubility in the hydrocarbon phase (Benzene or Toluene) indicating average deviations around 
5.0 % according to Folas et al. [26], over a wide range of temperature conditions. As for the MEG-
Toluene binary system, it can be seen through the Table 2.6, that CPA EoS with BETCR combining 
rules performs satisfactorily in predicting either the Toluene solubility in glycol-rich phase (7.5 % 
and 9.7% deviations) or the MEG solubility in the hydrocarbon-rich phase (16.4 % or 11.5 % 
deviations) according to Folas et al. [26] , [27]. Regarding the MEG-Benzene binary system, 
considering the deviations provided in the same Table 2.6, it can be seen that CPA EoS with BETCR 
combining rules performs better in the prediction of MEG solubility in the hydrocarbon-rich phase 
indicating 4.3 % deviation in contrast to the corresponding Benzene solubility in the glycol-rich phase 
with 9.7 % deviation, according to Folas et al. [27]. 
Furthermore, due to the main purpose of this study, which is the evaluation and comparison 
of performance of CPA and PC-SAFT EoS in hydrate inhibitor systems, the ternary and multi-
component systems containing the relevant components are of great interest. After conducting this 
literature review, it can be demonstrated that modeling work and corresponding conclusions regarding 
such systems is scarce. Additionally, only studies using CPA EoS found providing average deviations 
obtained after the modeling work. Thereafter, considering such deviations that are tabulated in Table 
2.7, it can be concluded that CPA EoS is a flexible thermodynamic tool for VLE and LLE of aqueous 
systems containing alcohols/glycols and aliphatic/aromatic hydrocarbons. CPA can predict very well 
the Water and the Methanol/Ethanol solubility in the aqueous phase or the hydrocarbon (Benzene or 
Toluene) solubility in the hydrocarbon phase in ternary systems containing Methanol, Ethanol, Water 
and Benzene/Toluene according to Folas et al. [26], indicating deviations ranged from 0.5 % up to 
7.0 %. Additionally, it was also highlighted the performance of the model in predicting the 
hydrocarbon solubility in the aqueous phase (20.0 % - 60.0 % deviations) and the Water or 
Methanol/Ethanol solubility in the hydrocarbon-rich phase (33.0 % - 50.0 % and 12 % - 50 % 
respectively). A similar performance of the CPA was obtained when applied in ternary systems 
containing MEG, Water and Benzene or Toluene. CPA was found to perform satisfactorily in 
predicting the MEG and Water solubility in the aqueous phase (less than 2.0 % deviations) and the 
hydrocarbon solubility in the hydrocarbon-rich phase (almost 0 % deviations), whereas the 
corresponding predictions for the hydrocarbon solubility in the aqueous phase (10.0 % - 25.0 % 
deviations) and the MEG solubility in the hydrocarbon-rich phase (7.5 % - 23.0 % deviations) 
according to Folas et al [27], were found to be higher due to the low mutual solubilities of 
==PAGE:44==
Technical University of Denmark 
 
44 
 
hydrocarbons with the polar components and the high uncertainties of the experimental data, because 
of the difficulties in measuring the low solubilities through experiments.  
Some additional conclusions, regarding CPA EoS in particular, were extracted, considering 
the discussion made by Kontogeorgis in Thermodynamic Models for Industrial Applications – From 
Classical and Advanced Mixing Rules to Association Theories [32]: 
 The performance of CPA EoS, when applied in mixtures containing alcohols or water with 
alkanes, was evaluated resulting in excellent binary VLE, LLE and SLE predictions and 
VLLE predictions for Alkanes-Water-Methanol systems as well. The reliability of the model 
in predicting the methanol partition coefficients of multicomponent systems was also 
demonstrated for a wide range of conditions (temperatures & pressures), by using only binary 
(temperature-independent) interaction parameters.  
  Phase equilibria of systems containing Glycols with Benzene/Toluene/Ethylbenzene/Xylene 
can be modeled satisfactorily by the CPA EoS, by using the CR-1 rule, if the solvation 
between the polar components and the aforementioned hydrocarbons was specifically taken 
into account.  
 CPA EoS was also appeared to be capable of correlating accurately the MEG solubility even 
in the case of binary interaction parameter was obtained from the Methane solubility in MEG 
at different temperature conditions.  
 Furthermore, CPA model with the Elliott’s rule can satisfactorily predict multicomponent 
aqueous mixtures containing either Methanol or MEG, which are the most widely used gas 
hydrate inhibitors. 
 The successfully accomplished simulations of Hydrocarbon-Glycol and Water-Glycol 
systems over a wide range of temperature conditions as well as the demonstrated predictive 
capability of the CPA EoS, when applied to multicomponent, multiphase equilibria, is the 
main reason why this model is of great interest in the oil & gas industry. 
 Moreover, MEG and Water solubility in the gas phase can be precisely predicted by using the 
CPA model at low temperatures and over a wide range of temperatures for the ternary system 
containing Methane, Water and MEG. 
Considering all the above-mentioned observations, it can be concluded the importance of 
conducting such a study, which will try to evaluate individually and also compare the performance 
of both models (CPA and PC-SAFT), when applied to hydrate inhibitor systems. 
==PAGE:45==
Modeling of Thermodynamics of Hydrate Inhibitor Systems 
 
45 
 
2.3 
Proposed Research Plan 
The basic purpose of this study is a fair comparison of CPA and PC-SAFT EoS in well – 
defined ternary systems containing Aliphatic and Aromatic hydrocarbons, Water, Methanol, Ethanol 
and MEG, as well as the evaluation of both models individually. By taking into consideration all the 
experimental phase equilibrium data from the 1st part of the literature review as well as the 
conclusions, presented above, from the 2nd part of the literature review, which was based on the 
evaluation of CPA and PC-SAFT models, it can be supported the importance of this study for the 
petroleum and chemical industries.   
Thus, considering the great interest of such systems, the applicability of each model in terms 
of accuracy and predictive correlation between experimental and modeling phase equilibrium data 
will be mainly investigated. Furthermore, after the accomplishment of this evaluation of the two 
aforementioned models, a discussion regarding the improvement in the modeling predictions will 
take place as well. As it was mentioned before, this evaluation will include systems containing 
Hydrocarbons (Aliphatic and Aromatic) with Water and Methanol, Ethanol or MEG. More 
specifically, high priority will be given in modeling systems containing Methane, Hexane, Benzene, 
Toluene, Water, Methanol, Ethanol and MEG. 
  The large experimental phase equilibrium data collection permits the modeling of several 
ternary and multi-component systems over a wide range of conditions (pressure and temperature). In 
the forthcoming modeling section of the study, apart from critical properties and modelling 
parameters, also binary interaction parameters are to be used in order to model the ternary & multi-
component systems. These binary interaction parameters will be taken either from literature review 
or by modeling these binaries and obtaining them. In order to be accomplished that further literature 
review will be conducted for phase equilibrium data of the binary systems this time. 
After having collected all the necessary parameters for the modeling of the ternary and multi-
component systems, the correlation between experimental data and the obtained ones from the 
modeling procedure will be conducted. By using these correlations and deviations, it will be possible 
the evaluation of both models and the demonstration of potential limitations that any of the models 
might present. 
Finally, an overall fair comparison between CPA and PC-SAFT will be conducted considering 
all previous correlations and possible suggestions will be demonstrated for improving the models.

Chapter 3: Modeling Work 
3.1 Pure Components Parameters 
3.1.1 Literature review for collecting Critical Properties & Model Parameters 
Before conducting any modeling work with thermodynamic phase equilibrium data, the 
corresponding parameters of the different models – used, for the pure components, have to be found 
through literature review.  
In this study two thermodynamic models were used, CPA and PC-SAFT EoS, thus in the 
following tables are illustrated the parameters found and selected for each model throughout the 
conducted literature review.  
In Table 3.2, the CPA parameters that will be used in this study are presented with their 
corresponding reference. As for the PC-SAFT model, various parameter sets have been proposed for 
associating fluids and in this study two different sets of parameters were chosen for Water, Methanol, 
Ethanol and MEG.  
In Table 3.3, both the parameters of the non – associating compounds and the associating ones 
(including two parameter sets for each of the aforementioned associating fluid) are presented with 
their corresponding references as well.  The choice of two sets of parameters for the associating 
components of PC-SAFT EoS was based on the fact that obtaining the best parameter set for such 
compounds is a great challenge. There are many different sets of parameters for these compounds 
and in order to be able to find the best among all, it has to be investigated their use by taking into 
consideration several criteria. In this study, it will also be investigated whether the phase equilibrium 
data can be used as a criteria to compare two sets of parameters. 
Additionally, the critical properties (Critical Temperature, Critical Pressure and Acentric 
Factor) of the aforementioned pure components that were contained in the systems of interest are also 
presented in the beginning of this section (Table 3.1).

3.1.2 Validation of Model Parameters for Polar Components with Vapor Pressure 
After collecting the parameters for each model, the procedure of validating the parameters of 
the polar components (Water, Methanol, Ethanol and MEG) was performed, by using the saturated 
pressures from the literature. In the following table (Table 3.4) are illustrated the deviations obtained 
by using the above – presented CPA parameters and the two sets of PC-SAFT parameters. 
Furthermore, the corresponding plots of Saturated Pressure vs. Temperature [ln(Psat) vs. (1/T)] are 
also provided afterwards for these four components in order to support the selection of these sets of 
parameters (Figures 3.1 – 3.4).   
Table 3.4: Average deviations obtained for the Model Parameters according to validating the Vapor Pressure 
Average Percentage Deviations of Vapor Pressure 
 Polar Components 
Range of Reduced Temperature 
CPA EoS 
PC-SAFT (Set 1) EoS

Considering the above – presented modeling results, both average deviations obtained and 
ln(Psat) – 1/T plots presented, it can be concluded that the selected sets of model parameters can be 
used for the further modeling work in binary and ternary systems. Regarding the forthcoming 
modeling work, both parameter sets for the PC-SAFT EoS were used, the former one will be 
mentioned as PC-SAFT (Set 1) and the latter one as PC-SAFT (Set 2). 
Finally, it has to be stated that the procedure of validating the parameters for the polar 
components resulted in similar performance of both models used. 
All the saturated pressures that were considered as criteria of validating the parameters of the 
models were found at NIST Standard Reference Data [41].

3.2 Binary Systems 
In order to perform any modeling of phase equilibrium data for ternary systems, the modeling 
of the corresponding binary systems are in general performed in advance. Every ternary system 
contains three components and in order to be modeled, the binary interaction parameters of the three 
different combinations of the components have to be known. In this study, these necessary binary 
interaction parameters were either collected through literature review, or by modeling the binary 
systems in order to obtain them.  
As for the CPA EoS, the interaction parameters were found through literature review, 
however, in some cases, the validation of these parameters was performed or modeling work was 
conducted in obtaining these parameters.  
As for PC-SAFT EoS, for both sets of parameters that were used, the binary interaction 
parameters were obtained either from literature review or by modeling binary phase equilibrium data.  
The first binary systems that were modeled in order to obtain the corresponding interaction 
parameters, which were required for the ternary modeling procedure, were all possible combinations 
of the polar components that were common in all the ternaries. Thereafter, at first, the binary 
interaction parameters of Water – Methanol, Water – Ethanol and Water – MEG, which were obtained 
or found, are illustrated below.  
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
==PAGE:58==
Technical University of Denmark 
 
58 
 
3.2.1 Water – Methanol 
For the binary system Water - Methanol, the CPA interaction parameter was found to be equal 
to -0.09, according to CERE ThermoSystem [26]. The binary interaction parameters for PC-SAFT 
(Set 1) and PC-SAFT (Set 2) were obtained, through modeling phase equilibrium data. The obtained 
values were found to be equal to -0.059 for the former and -0.063 for the latter one. The obtained 
average absolute deviations in Pressure from the modeling of that binary system are provided below.

PC-SAFT EoS (Set 1) and PC-SAFT EoS (Set 2), in order to evaluate the performance of the models 
in terms of accuracy, it can be concluded that all models correlate satisfactorily the aforementioned 
binary systems’ phase equilibrium data. More specifically, all average absolute pressure deviations 
were appeared to be below 4.0 %, so consequently the correlation between experimental and 
calculated data can be characterized as satisfactory.

was also performed modeling of binary systems containing hydrocarbons (Methane & n-Hexane) 
with polar components (Water, Methanol & MEG).

The Methane – Water binary system in particular can be characterized as a special type of 
binary system, due to the required temperature – dependent binary interaction parameters for 
obtaining good phase equilibrium correlations. Throughout this study, it was tested the proposed by 
CERE ThermoSystem [26] temperature – dependent Equation 3.1, which was resulted in average 
==PAGE:67==
Modeling of Thermodynamics of Hydrate Inhibitor Systems 
 
67 
 
pressure deviations of 8.2 %. Furthermore, throughout this study, the experimental phase equilibrium 
data found for that system through the literature review were also modeled in order to obtain the 
optimum binary interaction parameters for each temperature, indicating an average deviation of 5.3 
%. Moreover, these individual values of binary interaction parameters were plotted with respect to 
the temperature and the corresponding equation of the trend line (via Excel) was extracted and 
presented above (Eq. 3.2). As for the two sets of PC-SAFT EoS, both of them were modeled and the 
optimum binary interaction parameters were extracted, indicating average deviations in pressure 5.3 
% for the PC-SAFT EoS (Set 1) and 5.5 % for the PC-SAFT EoS (Set 2). Likewise CPA EoS, also 
for both two sets of Water parameters for PC-SAFT EoS similar equations were extracted and used 
afterwards in the modeling of the binary system in order to obtain deviations in pressure and 
correspondingly to be able to compare both models based on fair criteria and conditions. The obtained 
equations for the temperature – dependency of the binary interaction parameter of Methane – Water

==PAGE:69==
Modeling of Thermodynamics of Hydrate Inhibitor Systems 
 
69 
 
Considering all the above – presented average deviations and discussion, it can be concluded 
that by using the optimum obtained values of binary interaction parameters none of the two models 
(CPA vs. PC-SAFT) appears to have a significant better performance from the other one. More 
specifically, CPA EoS with the optimum binary interaction parameters showed an average deviation 
in pressure of 5.3 %, which was the same with the average deviation of PC-SAFT EoS (Set 1) and 
almost the same with the PC-SAFT EoS (Set 2) that was 5.5 %.  
As a more general comment, but with higher importance, is that the binary system Methane – 
Water in order to be modeled needs the implementation of temperature – dependent binary interaction 
parameters. This conclusion was extracted by using the average values of the corresponding models 
of the above – presented tables. So for CPA EoS it was used the average value (0.0224) of the third 
column of Table 3.11, where the proposed by CERE ThermoSystem [26] parameters were presented. 
As for the two sets of PC-SAFT EoS, the average values of the, obtained in this work, interaction 
parameters that are presented in Table 3.12, were used. For PC-SAFT (Set 1) was 0.0041 and for PC-
SAFT (Set 2) was -0.0731. However, the extremely high deviations obtained (more than 20.0 % in 
average absolute pressure in most cases) supported the conclusion of need for temperature – 
dependency as for the binary interaction parameters of that system. As for the use of zero interaction 
parameter, it resulted as well in higher than 20.0 % deviations for both models and in particular for 
PC-SAFT (Set 2) in large deviations and calculation failures for many points, thus a non-zero value 
is definitely required. 
The aforementioned temperature – dependency for the binary interaction parameters of 
Methane – Water system over the range of temperature conditions of this study resulted relatively 
same performance of both model. This fact can be supported from the similar obtained deviations 
(ranging from 7.5 % to 8.2 % in average absolute pressure deviation) by using both CPA and PC-
SAFT models and are illustrated in Table 3.13.  
 
 
 
 
==PAGE:70==
Technical University of Denmark 
 
70

The average values from the obtained ones were used again in order to be investigated the 
implementation of a temperature – independent interaction parameter for the two sets of PC-SAFT 
model as well. By using 0.045 for PC-SAFT (Set 1) and 0.0185 for PC-SAFT (Set 2), the obtained 
average deviations (6.3 % and 6.9 % respectively) proved the applicability of using these 
aforementioned temperature-independent interaction parameters for the binary system Methane – 
Methanol. Thus, in terms of accuracy, PC-SAFT (Set 1) EoS indicated the best results with average 
absolute deviations in pressure of 6.3 %, followed by PC-SAFT (Set 2) EoS with 6.9 % while CPA 
EoS showed 8.0 %. By using zero value for the kij the average deviations obtained were: 21.0 % for 
CPA EoS, 34.1 % for PC-SAFT (Set 1) EoS and 17.8 % for PC-SAFT (Set 2) EoS.

Regarding the binary system Methane – MEG and in terms of temperature dependency of its 
binary interaction parameter, it can be concluded that it is not required such a parameter. The 
temperature independent parameters obtained throughout this study can describe the phase equilibria 
of the aforementioned system, while indicating satisfactory average pressure deviations. CPA EoS 
with the suggested by CERE ThermoSystem [26] binary interaction parameter (0.1786) showed 
average deviations of 8.3 % in pressure, whereas the obtained from this work 0.17 binary interaction 
parameter showed slightly better correlation of the experimental data, indicating average pressure 
deviation of 6.3 %. Both sets of PC-SAFT EoS were used in modeling the experimental phase 
equilibrium data and the deviations obtained were 5.8 % for PC-SAFT (Set 1) and 8.1 % for PC-
SAFT (Set 2). Regarding the individual deviations obtained and presented in Table 3.15, it can be 
observed that the 1st set of data was the main reason for the relatively high deviations and was 
observed in both models used. The use of zero value for the binary interaction parameter for this 
system is out of discussion, due to the obtained deviations above 45.0 % for all models used and more 
specifically: CPA-> 56.4 %, PC-SAFT (Set 1)-> 49.4 % and PC-SAFT (Set 2)-> 46.2 %.

For the modeling work of the following binary systems, it was followed a different procedure 
and solvation was also taken into consideration.  
Thus, regarding CPA EoS, apart from the binary interaction parameter (kij) that was used in 
all systems before, now an extra interaction parameter was introduced, the cross-association volume 
(βcross).  
Likewise CPA, also in PC-SAFT EoS, apart from the binary interaction parameter (kij), an 
additional parameter was also introduced, the fitted associated volume (𝜅𝑓𝑖𝑡𝑡𝑒𝑑
𝐴𝐵
).    
More specifically, the kij in these systems was adjusted manually, whereas the corresponding 
associated volume parameters were obtained through optimization. 
Thereafter, the following binary systems were modeled with accounting solvation and two 
interaction parameters were presented: 
 Benzene – Water 
 Benzene – MEG  
 Benzene – Methanol 
 Toluene – Water  
 Toluene – MEG

By taking into consideration the above – presented table with average absolute deviations in 
pressure of the modeling work for the binary phase equilibrium data found through the literature 
review and by also including the results (plots) of modeling the n-Hexane – Water, the n-Hexane – 
MEG and the n-Hexane – Methanol binary systems, it can be concluded that both CPA and PC-SAFT 
models performed satisfactory in correlating the binary phase equilibrium data. Furthermore, it was 
not observed a significantly better performance in terms of accuracy for one of the models. As it was 
discussed in details in that section, in some binaries CPA performed better than PC-SAFT and vice 
versa in the rest. However, the obtained individual average absolute deviations for each binary did 
not result in a general superior performance of one of the two models. It should also be mentioned 
that in order to be able to make a more clear conclusion about the performance of both models further 
investigation has to be done in wider temperature and pressure ranges. Finally, it has to be

3.3 Ternary Systems 
In this section of the study are presented all the ternary hydrate inhibitor systems that were 
modeled by using the CPA and PC-SAFT EoS, as well as the evaluation of the models – used 
according to the deviations obtained.  
The ternary hydrate inhibitor systems that were modeled in this study are listed below: 
 
Water – Methanol – Methane  
 
Water – MEG – Methane 
 
Water – MEG – n-Hexane  
 
Water – Methanol – n-Hexane 
 
Water – MEG – Benzene 
 
Water – Methanol – Benzene 
 
Water – MEG – Toluene 
 
In all the forthcoming presented ternary systems, the modeling work was conducted according 
to the phase composition data that were available. Because there were cases that only the liquid phase 
composition was mentioned and presented in the corresponding literature source.

Modeling of Thermodynamics of Hydrate Inhibitor Systems

Considering the above – presented table, as well as the previous section of the Methane – 
Water – Methanol ternary system and the Methane – Water binary system’s section, it can be 
concluded that the proposed by CERE ThermoSystem [26] equation for the temperature – dependency 
of the binary interaction parameter for the Methane – Water system even though if it was slightly 
worse in the binary phase equilibrium data correlation, appeared to be more precise when the 
investigated system is ternary. Of course this conclusion could be further investigated by using wider 
temperature range conditions both for the binary system as well as for the ternary ones and more 
experimental phase equilibrium data for the corresponding systems. As for the evaluation of the two 
models (CPA and PC-SAFT), it can be concluded that CPA shows a slightly better performance in 
predicting the methane mole fraction in the liquid phase approx. 5.0 % less than both sets of PC-
SAFT EoS used.

absolute deviations of both models decreased approx. 10.0 % by using a temperature – independent

The presented table above shows the average deviations obtained, by taking into account all 
phase equilibrium data that were presented before (Table 3.50). However, due to observations made 
by plotting the data, likewise the previous ternary (n-Hexane – Water – MEG), the reliability of the 
==PAGE:112==
Technical University of Denmark 
 
112 
 
experimental data had to be investigated. In order to show the observed problem, two figures 
representing mole fractions of all components in both phase with CPA EoS are presented below, one 
at 293.2 K [28] and one at 298.15 K [24]. 
 
Figure 3.40: CPA predictions of molar fractions of all components of n-Hexane – Water – Methanol Ternary System at 
293.20 K in both phases with respect to the mole fraction of Methanol in polar phase (Experimental data [28]) 
 
In the above – presented figure, it can be seen that CPA EoS predicts satisfactorily the mole 
fractions of all components in both phases. However, it can also be observed through the plot that the 
mole fraction of Water in the Hydrocarbon-rich phase is approximately equal to 0.001. In contrast to 
that observation, in the following figure, which is also a representation of CPA EoS performance in 
the same ternary system but in a slightly higher temperature, it can be seen that the model also predicts 
a mole fraction of Water in the same range of values (around 0.001). The plotted experimental points 
of the Water mole fraction in Hydrocarbon-phase appear to be in a higher value around 0.01. Thus, 
further investigation has to be done as for the reliability of the literature – obtained experimental 
phase equilibrium data. 
==PAGE:113==
Modeling of Thermodynamics of Hydrate Inhibitor Systems 
 
113 
 
 
Figure 3.41: CPA predictions of molar fractions of all components of n-Hexane – Water – Methanol Ternary System at 
298.15 K in both phases with respect to the mole fraction of Methanol in polar phase (Experimental data [24]) 
In order to judge, whether the experimental mole fractions of Water in Hydrocarbon-rich 
phase are erroneous or not, the corresponding binary systems has to be checked also. Considering the 
modeling work in the binary n-Hexane – Water system, it can be concluded by observing the 
experimental values of the Water mole fraction in n-Hexane phase and also by taking into 
consideration the presented x – T figure in that section that the value of the mole fraction of Water in 
the Hydrocarbon phase was ranging below 0.001, thus the experimental values around 0.01 can be 
characterized as doubtful.  
Thereafter, due to the fact that the only reliable experimental data were at only one 
temperature (293.2 K), the evaluation of both models in order to be fair should include a wider 
temperature condition range. However, it is presented below the table with the obtained deviations in 
the mole fractions of the components of that ternary system based only on the reliable data at 293.2 
K.  
==PAGE:114==

aqueous – rich phase, whereas both sets of PC-SAFT show average absolute deviations approx. 20.0 
% higher. Regarding the hydrocarbon – rich phase, CPA and PC-SAFT (Set 2) perform similarly, 
whereas PC-SAFT (Set 1) remains relatively the worst among all.

Considering both above – presented tables with the obtained deviations for each of the two 
investigated cases (solvation and no – solvation), it can be concluded that the influence of 
implementing the concept of solvation between Benzene and Methanol also for the ternary system 
did not result in better predictions. By using any of the models it can be observed that the predictions 
are almost the same, thus it can be concluded that when a ternary system containing Benzene and 
Methanol is investigated, no – solvation between the two aforementioned compounds has to be taken 
into account. The same observation was extracted in the binary Benzene – Methanol section as for 
the binary system.  
As for the comparison of the models, it can be seen from the tables with the deviations that all 
models (CPA and both sets of PC-SAFT) perform almost the same indicating close values of 
deviations for all predicted molar fractions. Moreover, it has to be mentioned that, relatively to other 
ternaries, high deviations were obtained as for the mole fractions of Water in the aqueous – rich phase 
and of Benzene in hydrocarbon – rich phase. The also relatively high deviations of Methanol in both 
phases can be seen in the following partition coefficients plots and especially at 318.15 K.

3.3.8 Summary of the Ternary Systems   
In this section of the study are presented summarized the obtained deviations throughout the 
modeling work that was done in the investigated ternary systems. Furthermore, the extracted main 
conclusions as for the evaluation of the thermodynamic models that were used is also taking place. 
The first two ternary systems that were modeled in this work were Methane – Water – 
Methanol and Methane – Water – MEG. Throughout the modeling of these two ternary systems, two 
cases were investigated based on the temperature – dependency or not of the binary interaction 
parameter of Methane – Water. In contrast to the modeling of the binary Methane – Water system 
that resulted in a need of temperature – dependency of the binary interaction parameter in order to 
achieve better correlation with the experimental phase equilibrium data, when the modeling came to 
the ternary systems a different observation was extracted. As it can be seen in the following two 
figures (the former one for the Methane – Water – Methanol and the latter one for the Methane – 
Water – MEG), the use of temperature – independent value as for the binary interaction parameter of 
the Methane – Water system, resulted in better predictions with all models used. More specifically, 
in Figure 3.53, are illustrated the obtained average absolute deviations of mole fractions of Methane 
in liquid phase, Water in vapor phase and Methanol in liquid phase as well.  
 
Figure 3.53: Average Absolute Deviations in mole fractions for the Ternary Methane – Water – Methanol System

In the following Figure 3.54, the obtained average absolute deviations in the liquid mole 
fraction of Methane in the Methane – Water – MEG ternary system are highlighted. 
 
Figure 3.54: Average Absolute Deviations in Liquid Mole Fraction of Methane for the Ternary Methane – Water – 
MEG System 
Considering both above – presented bar charts, it can be concluded that the use of temperature 
– independent kij for the binary Methane – Water resulted in better predictions with both CPA and 
PC-SAFT models in both investigated ternary systems. The similarity that was obtained in both 
ternaries was that, by the use of the aforementioned temperature – independent binary interaction 
parameter, the average absolute deviation in the mole fraction of Methane in the liquid phase 
decreased significantly (approx. 10.0 %). Moreover, as for the evaluation of the two thermodynamic 
models that were used, it can be concluded that PC-SAFT was slightly better in predicting the mole 
fractions of the Methane – Water – Methanol ternary systems (approx. 4.0 % better than CPA), 
whereas CPA appeared to be slightly better in predicting the mole fraction of Methane in the liquid 
phase in the ternary Methane – Water – MEG (approx. 5.0 % better than PC-SAFT). Such differences 
are not sufficient to conclude whether one of the two models performs better. Finally, as for the two 
different sets of PC-SAFT EoS, it can be concluded that their performance in overall was very similar. 
The following two ternaries that were modeled contained n-Hexane as the hydrocarbon, 
whereas the rest components remained the same. In the following bar chart, the average absolute 
deviations in mole fractions for both ternaries are presented combined in the same figure (left part: 
n-Hexane – Water – MEG and right part: n-Hexane – Water – Methanol).

Figure 3.55: Average Absolute Deviations in mole fractions for the Ternary Systems: Left: n-Hexane – Water – MEG 
and Right: n-Hexane – Water – Methanol 
 
The fluctuation of the deviations in the several liquid mole fractions that were obtained after 
the modeling of these two ternary systems support the previous conclusion as for the difficulty in 
characterizing one of the two models as “superior” over the other. By taking into consideration the n-
Hexane – Water – MEG (left part of the figure), it can be concluded that PC-SAFT (Set 2) was overall 
the best model in predicting the phase equilibrium data. On the other hand, CPA appeared to be 
relatively better in overall for the predictions of the n-Hexane – Water – Methanol system. 
Furthermore, it should also be mentioned the significantly better performance of PC-SAFT (Set 2) 
over the PC-SAFT (Set 1) for both of the investigated systems. 
The last category of hydrocarbons that modeling work was performed on and predictions were 
recorded and compared with the experimental phase equilibrium data were the aromatic 
hydrocarbons, Benzene and Toluene. In the following Figure 3.56, the ternary systems Benzene – 
Water – MEG and Toluene – Water – MEG are presented together. The performance of both models 
in predicting the phase equilibrium data can be characterized as very satisfactory. Once again, also 
for these two ternaries, it can be concluded that both models perform similarly without superior 
performance of the one over the other. In overall, it can also be concluded that both sets of PC-SAFT 
performed almost the same.

The last ternary that is presented below is the Benzene – Water – Methanol system and the 
difference in that system was the investigation of two different cases. As it was also investigated in 
the Benzene – Methanol binary section, in the ternary Benzene – Water – Methanol the concept of 
solvation was also under investigation. Similarly to the binary, also in the ternary, the solvation 
between Benzene and Methanol did not result in better predictions as for the mole fractions, thus it 
can be concluded that no – solvation between the aforementioned compounds has to be taken into 
account, when both of them are present. 
As for the evaluation of the models, it can be concluded that for that system in particular, CPA 
appeared to perform slightly better than both sets of PC-SAFT in predicting the mole fractions of the 
Benzene – Water – Methanol ternary system. However, again the difference between the models’ 
performances was not that significant. Therefore, the conclusion that can be stated is that CPA 
performs slightly better in phase equilibrium calculations of that ternary system. The schematic 
representation that follows (bar chart) represents only the case of no – solvation between Benzene 
and Methanol and highlights the slightly better performance of CPA over both sets of PC-SAFT.

Chapter 4: Conclusions 
After conducting all the modeling work that was presented and discussed in details in the 
previous chapter of this study, in this chapter the concluding remarks that were extracted, by taking 
into consideration the obtained modeling results, are demonstrated. 
First of all, the basic purpose of this study was a fair comparison between CPA and PC-SAFT 
EoS in well-defined ternary systems including hydrocarbons, water and chemicals. By taking into 
consideration both binary and ternary systems, which were investigated in this study, it can be 
concluded that none of the models showed significantly better performance from the other one. Both 
models appeared to be capable of correlating the binary systems’ phase equilibrium data and 
predicting the corresponding ternary ones satisfactorily. More specifically, it has to be mentioned that 
there were binaries or ternaries that CPA was slightly better than PC-SAFT or vice versa, but after 
taking into account all the investigated systems, both models performed similarly and satisfactorily. 
As for the ternary hydrate inhibitor systems in particular, CPA and PC-SAFT EoS appeared 
to perform similarly good, providing accurate predictions for the phase equilibrium compositions. 
More specifically, CPA appeared slightly better than PC-SAFT in predicting the mole fraction of 
Methane in liquid phase for the Methane – Water – MEG, whereas the reverse observation was 
extracted for the Methane – Water – Methanol ternary system. PC-SAFT was also slightly better in 
the predictions of mole fractions of Methanol and Water in the vapor phase of the ternary Methane – 
Water – Methanol system. Moreover, CPA appeared to perform better in the corresponding 
predictions for the n-Hexane – Water – Methanol, whereas PC-SAFT (Set 2) performed better for the 
n-Hexane – Water – MEG system. In both aforementioned systems, PC-SAFT (Set 1) was relatively 
the worst model in terms of predictive capability. Finally, as for the aromatics’ part, both models once 
again showed insignificant differences as for their predictive capabilities. Furthermore, it was also 
observed a very good agreement between the obtained predictions and the experimental phase 
equilibrium compositions for Toluene – Water – MEG and Benzene – Water – MEG in particular. 
In overall, this “fair battle” that was investigated between CPA EoS and PC-SAFT EoS ended 
up without a clear winner, indicating the applicability of both models in correlating binary phase 
equilibrium data and in predicting the corresponding ternary phase equilibrium data of hydrate 
inhibitor systems containing hydrocarbons (Methane, n-Hexane, Benzene & Toluene), Water and 
chemicals (Methanol and MEG).  
==PAGE:136==
Technical University of Denmark 
 
136 
 
Regarding PC-SAFT EoS, in this study, two different sets of parameters were used in order 
to be investigated the predominance of one between the two as for the binary correlations and ternary 
predictions. Likewise the performance of the two models, also this comparison ended without 
resulting in a clear “winner”. Both sets performed similarly and the use of the phase equilibrium data 
can be concluded as not a criteria of evaluating the several proposed by different authors’ sets of 
parameters. In overall and by taking into consideration all investigated cases, it can be concluded that 
PC-SAFT (Set 2) was slightly better than PC-SAFT (Set 1) in the vast majority of the cases, however 
the deviations obtained by both sets of parameters were very close to each other.  
Furthermore, while performing the modeling work with binary and ternary systems containing 
both Methane and Water compounds, the temperature – dependency or temperature – independency 
of the binary interaction parameter for the Methane – Water system was investigated. Interestingly, 
this binary system has to be characterized as “special” or “unique”, due to the results obtained. The 
interesting observation throughout the modeling of that system is that a temperature – dependent 
binary interaction parameter correlates significantly better the binary phase equilibrium data, whereas 
the ternary predictions are considerably better with a temperature – independent binary interaction 
parameter for the same system.  
Apart from the two cases of binary interaction dependency of kij for Methane – Water, there 
was also another system that two cases were under investigation. It was investigated whether the 
solvation or not between Benzene and Methanol would result in better binary correlations and ternary 
predictions. After accomplishing the modeling of both cases, it can be concluded that the solvation 
between the aforementioned compounds did not provide better results, thus whenever both 
components are involved in a system for investigation no – solvation has to be taken into account. 
 
 
 
 
==PAGE:137==
Modeling of Thermodynamics of Hydrate Inhibitor Systems 
 
137 
 
Chapter 5: Future Work 
In this study, the systems that were investigated and modeled in order to evaluate the 
performance of CPA and PC-SAFT EoS were binary and ternary systems containing Methane, n-
Hexane, Benzene, Toluene, Water, Methanol and MEG. By adding more components in the under – 
investigation sample, the conclusions could remain the same or indicate a better model among two. 
Thereafter, the investigation of hydrate inhibitor systems containing also Ethane, n-Octane and 
Ethanol as well, could support the conclusion that both models perform similarly or label one of them 
as better. 
Apart from ternary systems, further investigation in quaternary or even in multi – component 
systems could be a good base of comparing both models. However, this research require also the 
corresponding phase equilibrium data that are sometimes scarce and not easy to be found.  
Regarding the special case of the temperature – dependency of the binary interaction 
parameter of Methane – Water, it can also be done further investigation. Apart from Methane – Water, 
also Ethane – Water appeared to require a temperature – dependent kij according to the literature 
review that was conducted. Therefore, the investigation of ternary systems containing Ethane, Water 
and Methanol/MEG could also be modeled in the future. 
Additionally, the temperature and pressure conditions of the systems that are investigated play 
a crucial role as for all the concluding remarks. It is an undeniable fact that the wider the range of 
temperature and pressure conditions is taking into account, the stronger the conclusion becomes. 
Thus, further modeling work over a wider range of conditions could also help the evaluation of the 
models. 
Staying in the same topic of wider range of temperature and pressure conditions, it has to be 
mentioned the difficulty in conducting experimental work in obtaining phase equilibrium data. 
However, further experimental work would give more phase equilibrium VLE, LLE and VLLE data 
that could be used for evaluating the same systems of interest. 
Considering the literature review conducted in this study, it should be mentioned that the vast 
majority of the ternaries modeled and published were by authors using CPA EoS. Thereafter, it could 
also be a good future goal for the scientific community to model and publish modeling results by 
using PC-SAFT EoS.
